The Mover and Subject Do Not Determine the Specific Type of Motion
Asserts that the unity of the mover and subject do not affect the specific type of motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the specific type of motion is not determined by the unity of the mover or the unity of the subject, and see how forced and natural motions can share the same type.

Core Idea
Different movers do not necessarily produce different types of motion.

This passage from Sharh al-Mawaqif addresses a common assumption: that the cause of motion determines its type. The author argues that neither the mover's identity nor the subject's identity affects the specific type of motion. He provides a clear example: a stone thrown upward and fire rising upward are the same type of motion despite having different movers.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and English translation carefully, noting the main claim and the example.
2
Identify the argument
The passage uses a logical argument: if a difference in mover does not cause individual difference, then it does not cause specific difference. Understand the reasoning and the example.
The example compares forced motion (stone) and natural motion (fire).
3
Consider the incomplete ending
The Arabic cuts off mid-sentence. Reflect on how the argument would likely conclude: that variation in the subject does not affect the specific type of motion either.
This reinforces the main point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا عبرة في الوحدة النوعية للحركة بوحدة المحرك لأن الأمور المختلفة بالنوع قد تشترك في نوع واحد من الأثر ولما مر من أن تعدد المحرك ولو بحسب النوع لا يوجب تعددا في الحركة بحسب الشخص وإذ لا يوجب اختلاف المحرك بحسب النوع اختلاف الشخص في الحركة فالنوع أولى بأن لا يوجبه ذلك الاختلاف لأن ما يوجب اختلاف النوع يوجب اختلاف الشخص بالضرورة من دون عكس كلي فحركة الحجر إلى العلو قسراً وحركة النار إليه طبعاً لا يختلف بالنوع من حيث هما كذلك أي من حيث استنادهما إلى محركين مختلفين بالنوع أعني القاسر والطبيعة بل هاتان الحركتان متفقتان في الماهية ولا عبرة أيضاً بوحدة ما له الحركة فإن تنوع المحل لا
And no consideration in the specific unity of motion is given to the unity of the mover, because things that differ in type may share one type of effect, and because of what has passed: that the multiplicity of the mover, even by type, does not cause a multiplicity in motion with respect to the individual; and since the difference of the mover by type does not cause the difference of the individual in motion, then all the more reason that it should not cause the type to differ, because that which causes difference in type necessarily causes difference in individual, but not conversely. Thus the motion of a stone upward by force and the motion of fire upward by nature do not differ in type from the perspective of being as such, i.e., from the perspective of their being attributed to two different movers in type, namely the violent and nature; rather these two motions are in agreement in essence. And also no consideration is given to the unity of that which has motion, for the variation of the subject does not...
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage discusses whether the unity of the mover or the unity of the subject influences the specific type of motion. It asserts that the specific unity of motion is not affected by the unity of the mover, because things that differ by type can share the same type of effect. The argument proceeds: if a difference in mover does not even cause individual (شخصي) difference in motion, then it is even less likely to cause specific (نوعي) difference. The reason is that what causes specific difference necessarily causes individual difference, but not vice versa. As an example, the motion of a stone thrown upward (forced motion) and the motion of fire rising upward (natural motion) are the same type, despite being driven by movers differing in type (violence vs nature). Then the passage adds that the unity of the subject (that which has motion) also does not affect the specific type, because variation in the subject (تنوع المحل) does not necessarily change the type (the sentence is cut off).

Key Terms
المحرك
المحل
الوحدة النوعية
الشخص
القاسر والطبيعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Different causes (e.g., natural vs forced) always produce different types of motion.
Correction: The passage shows that forced motion of a stone upward and natural motion of fire upward are the same type of motion, because the mover does not affect the specific type.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the motion of a stone thrown upward and the motion of fire rising upward considered the same type?
A) Because they have the same mover.
B) Because they have the same subject.
C) Because the mover does not affect the specific type of motion.
D) Because they are both natural.

Key Takeaway
The specific type of motion depends on the nature of the motion itself, not on the mover or the subject.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, do you judge the moral quality of an action by the type of action itself or by the person performing it? How might this passage's principle about motion challenge your tendency to focus on the doer rather than the deed?

Opposition of Movements: Subject and Goal
The author argues that opposition of movements depends on subject and goal, not just subject.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the opposition of movements in kalam is determined by both the subject in which they occur and the goal toward which they move, not just the subject alone.

Core Idea
Movement opposition is defined by both source and target, not just the moving body.

In this passage from al-Mawaqif, the author argues against a simplistic view that movements are opposite solely because of the bodies they inhere in. Using the example of ascending and descending—opposites even when occurring in the same body—he establishes that opposition hinges on both the subject (mā fī-hi) and the goal (mā ilay-hi). This principle is crucial for understanding causation in the physical world.

Guided Path
1
Read the main text and commentary
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. The main text gives the claim; the commentary explains it.
The commentary is essential for understanding the nuanced position.
2
Identify the two factors
Notice that the author explicitly states that opposition is not due solely to 'what they are in' but also 'what they are toward.' Find these terms in the text.
The Arabic terms are ما فيه and ما إليه.
3
Consider the objection from possibilities
The commentary mentions that in some materials opposition might be due to other factors, but this is dismissed as a mere possibility that does not affect the general rule.
This prepares for the next lesson's objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد الثامن : الحركات المتضادة بين الصاعدة والهابطة ] تضاد الحركات ليس لتضاد ما فيه فإن الصاعدة والهابطة ضدان ) بلا شبهة ( وإن اتحد ما فيه هاتان الحركتان وكذلك الحركة من السواد إلى البياض ضد للحركة من ( 
قوله : ( من أن الحركة المستديرة إلخ سواء كانت وضعية أو أينية فهو استدلال بالحكم العام على الخاص فلا مصادرة .
قوله : (تضاد الحركات إلخ) أي تضاد كل حركة مع أخرى ليس لأجل تضاد ما فيه فقط، لأنه يوجد في التصور بدون تضاد ما فيه وكذا الحال في التحرك والمحرك، بل تضاد كل حركة أخرى لأجل ما فيه وما إليه وأما كونه في بعض المواد لأجل ما منه وما إليه، وفي بعضها لتضاد مع أمور أخر فمجرد احتمال عقل لا يضر المقصود نعم لو تحقق التضاد في مادة ما بدون تضاد مه فيه وما إليه يضر فما أورده صاحب التجريد من أنه يجوز تعليل الواحد النوعي بعلل متعددة،
قوله : ( من أن الحركة المستديرة لا تضاد فيها بيان لما الذي هو عبارة عن الدليل فإن قلت : هذا نفس المدعى فكيف يكون بياناً لما الذي هو عبارة عن الدليل قلت : توصيف الحركة بالمستديرة إشعار بالدليل فالاستدارة هي التي بسببها لم يجر في الوصفية تضاد كما سيظهر.
قوله : ( فإن الصاعدة والهابطة ضدان وإن اتحد ما فيه اعترض عليه بأنه يجوز أن يكون لمعلول واحد علل متعددة يتحقق هذا المعلول بتحقق كل واحد منها، فتحقق المعلول صورة بدون ما يدعى دم عليته لا يدل على المدعى وهو عدم عليته مطلقاً لجواز تحققه
The eighth observation: Opposing movements between ascending and descending. The opposition of movements is not due to opposition of what they are in. For ascending and descending are two opposites, without doubt, even if what they are in is the same. Likewise, the movement from blackness to whiteness is opposite to the movement from [whiteness to blackness]...
His statement: (from that circular movement, etc.) whether it is positional or local, it is an inference from a general rule to a specific case, so there is no circularity.
His statement: (the opposition of movements, etc.) i.e., the opposition of each movement with another is not solely due to opposition of what they are in, because it exists conceptually without opposition of what they are in, and likewise for the mover and the moved. Rather, the opposition of each movement to another is due to what it is in and what it is toward. As for it being in some materials due to what it is from and what it is to, and in some due to opposition with other things, it is a mere rational possibility that does not harm the intended meaning. Indeed, if opposition were realized in some material without opposition of what it is in and what it is to, that would harm. So what the author of al-Tajrīd mentioned, that it is permissible to explain a single specific effect by multiple causes...
His statement: (that circular movement has no opposition) is an explanation of what is the proof. For if you say: this is the very claim, so how can it be an explanation of what is the proof? I say: describing movement as circular suggests the proof, for circularity is that due to which no opposition occurs in positional movement, as will appear.
His statement: (for ascending and descending are opposites even if what they are in is the same) An objection was raised against him: it is permissible that a single effect has multiple causes, such that this effect is realized by the realization of each of them. So the realization of the effect in a certain form without what is claimed to be its cause does not prove the claim that it is absolutely not a cause, because it is possible that it is realized...
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is the eighth observation, arguing that the opposition of movements is not due to the thing in which they occur (e.g., the body), but due to both the subject and the goal. The main text gives the example of ascending and descending: they are opposites even when occurring in the same body. The commentary first clarifies that circular movement (whether positional or local) has no opposition, and that citing this is not circular reasoning but an inference from general to specific. Then it explains that opposition of movements is due to the 'what they are in' (the subject) and 'what they are toward' (the goal), not just the subject. It allows that in some materials, opposition may be due to other factors, but that is a mere possibility. If there were a case of opposition without opposition of subject and goal, that would be problematic. The commentary then addresses an objection from the author of al-Tajrīd: it is possible that a single effect has multiple causes, so the existence of a movement without a certain cause does not prove that cause is unnecessary. The passage ends mid-argument, explaining that the existence of an effect without a claimed cause does not negate the claim of causality absolutely, because the effect could be realized by another cause. The full answer may continue on the next page.

ما فيه
ما إليه
حركة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that ascending and descending are opposites only because they occur in different bodies or that opposition is purely a function of the moving body.
Correction: The text shows they are opposites even in the same body, so opposition must also depend on the direction (goal).

Checkpoint
What example does the author use to show that opposition of movements is not solely due to the subject?
A) Circular movement
B) Ascending and descending in the same body
C) Movement from blackness to whiteness
D) Local motion

Key Takeaway
Opposition of movements depends on both the subject and the goal; the subject alone does not determine opposition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your daily life, do you pay more attention to what you do (the subject of your actions) or to why you do it (the goal)? How does this lesson's insight that opposition depends on both subject and goal challenge you to examine your intentions behind actions that might outwardly appear similar?
?
Think of a time when you were certain you were right because your action was 'correct'—but the result was conflict. Could the real opposition have been in the goal you were pursuing rather than in the act itself? What would change if you realigned your goal with sincerity?
?
If the goal of a movement defines its opposition, then the goal of your life's movement defines its direction. Are you aware of what your ultimate goal is? Take a moment to honestly name one area where your goal might be misaligned with truth, and commit to adjusting it today.

The Objection from Multiple Causes
The objection: a single effect might have multiple causes, so absence of one cause does not negate its causal role.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that a single effect can have multiple causes, and why the absence of one cause does not disprove its potential causality.

Core Idea
Multiple possible causes can produce the same effect, complicating causal claims.

The author of al-Tajrīd raises a powerful objection against the argument that opposition is due to subject and goal. He notes that a single effect might be caused by multiple different causes. Therefore, if a movement occurs without a particular cause, that does not prove that cause is never effective. This lesson presents the objection and the beginning of the author's response.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection passage
This is a direct quote from the commentary where an objection is raised. Read the Arabic and translation carefully.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the full response is on the next page.
2
Understand the logic of the objection
The objector says: if an effect can have multiple causes, then the absence of one cause in a particular case does not prove that cause is never a cause. This challenges the earlier argument that if opposition occurs without difference in subject and goal, then subject and goal are not necessary.
This is a standard argument in Kalam about causality.
3
Ponder the beginning of the response
The commentary begins to reply but cuts off. Consider what a response might entail: perhaps distinguishing necessary vs. contingent causality, or noting that the objection only creates a possibility, not a proven counterexample.

Causality and Created Things
intermediate
8 min
The Opposition of Motions is from Their Termini, Not from the Substrate or Mover
Proves that opposition of motions is from their termini.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the opposition of two motions is due to the opposition of their starting and ending points (the from- and to- termini), not due to the substrate or the mover, and how the proof works with examples.

Core Idea
The opposition of motions is determined by their beginnings and ends, not by the substance or the agent.

In this lesson, we examine a key proof in kalam physics: why two motions are considered opposites. The author argues that the real cause is not the thing in which motion occurs (the substrate) nor the moving force, but rather the opposition of the from-point and to-point. We will see this through examples like rising and falling air, and motion from black to white.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and its translation to grasp the overall argument. Notice the structure: claim, evidence, objection, response.
2
Identify the main claim
The passage opens by stating that opposition of motions is not due to opposition of what the motion occurs in (mā fīhi) nor due to opposition of the mover (al-muḥarrik).
This is the thesis to be proved.
3
Examine the evidence
Two examples are given: (1) rising and falling motions of air are opposites even though the substrate (air) is the same; (2) motion from black to white is opposite to motion from white to black even if the path is identical. Also, natural motions from a single nature (air rising from earth's region and falling from fire's region) are opposites despite the same mover.
These examples show that opposition does not require difference in substrate or mover.
4
Understand the objection and response
An objection from some thinkers (al-Rāzī and Ibn Sīnā) claims that rising and falling are not truly opposites because they end at a single limit (being above water and below fire). The author counters this by showing that if such extreme difference were required, many motions (like a stone's motion) would not be considered opposites, which is false.
The response emphasizes that the real cause is opposition of the from- and to-points.
5
Grasp the conclusion
The passage concludes that all opposition of motions is due to opposition of mā minhu wa mā ilayhi (what is from and what is to), and this is the correct analysis.
This aligns with the induction and the use of the verbal noun in the general sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصد الثامن : الحركات المتضادة الصاعدة والهابطة تضاد الحركات ليس لتضاد ما فيه فإن الصاعدة والهابطة ضدان بلا شبهة وإن اتحد ما فيه هاتان الحركتان وكذلك الحركة من السواد إلى البياض ضد للحركة من البياض إلى السواد وإن فرض وحدة الطريق أعني وحدة ما فيه ( ولا لتضاد المحرك لتضاد ) الحركتين ( الطبيعيتين) الصادرتين عن طبيعة واحدة فإن الهواء إذا حصل في حيز الأرض صعد عنه طبعاً، وإذا حصل في حيز النار هبط عنه كذلك فبين هذه الصاعدة والهابطة تضاد مع وحدة المحرك وهذا المثال إنما يصح إذا لم يعتبر في التضاد غاية الخلاف كما يظهر من كلام الإمام في الملخص والمذكور في السماء والعالم من كتاب الشفاء أن هاتين الحركتين ليستا متضادتين كما ظن بعضهم، لأنهما تنتهيان إلى طرف واحد وتوجيهه على ما في المباحث المشرقية أن الضدين يجب أن يكون بينهما غاية التباعد ، ولم يوجد ذلك في هاتين الحركتين، لأن البعد بين حركة النار وحركة الأرض أكثر من البعد بين صعود الهواء عن المركز وهبوطه عن المحيط، وكيف يكونان متضادين والمطلوب بهما حالة واحدة هي أن تكون فوق الماء وتحت النار ويرد عليه أنه يلزم منه أن لا يكون تضاد في الحركات الأينية إلا الصاعدة الواصلة إلى المحيط والهابطة الواصلة إلى المركز ، فلا تكون حركة الحجر فيجوز أن يكون التضاد في بعض الصور لتضاد ما فيه وما إليه، وفي بعض التضاد ما فيه أو المحرك أو المتحرك إنما يردان لو كان المقصود الاستدلال بانتفاء التضاد لأجل الأمور المذكورة في بعض الصور على ثبوته في جميع الصور، لأجل تضاد ما فيه وما إليه، بل المقصود بيان الواقع وتحقيقه أن كل صورة يتحقق التضاد بين الحركات لا يكون بدون تضاد ما منه وما إليه سواء كان معه تضاد آخر أو لا قوله : ( وإن فرض وحدة الطريق) بأن يكون الطريق من البياض إلى السواد ومن الزيادة إلى النقصان بعينه الطريق من السواد إلى البياض ومن النقص إلى الزيادة وبالجملة هي المتوسطات بأعيانها كما أن المسافة في النزول هي المسافة في الصعود كذا في الشفاء قوله تنتهيان إلى طرف (واحد فلا يكون بينهما التضاد بحسب المنتهى، ولا بد تضاد الحركتين كل من المبدأ والمنتهي جميع تضاد تلك الصورة بعلة أخرى، وبهذا ظهر ما في تعليل انتفاء تضاد الحركات بتضاد المتحرك. وفي تعليل انتفاء تضادها بتضاد المحرك من الخلل والجواب أنه قد تقرر من قواعدهم أن المصدر المضاف من صيغ العموم، فالمعنى جميع تضاد الحركات ليس لتضاد ما فيه فعلى هذا ينطبق الدليل على الدعوى فإن قلت انتفاء هذا الإيجاب الكلي لا يستلزم أن يكون الحركات بحسب ما منه وما إليه قلت : لم يدع أحد هذا الاستلزام بل إن الأمر في الواقع كذلك كما يدل عليه الاستقراء، فليتأمل. قوله : ( عن طبيعة واحدة فإن الطبيعة هي العلة الفاعلية للحركة والحالة الغير الملائمة ليست جزءاً من العلة الفاعلية ولهذا لم يذكرها هاهنا وإن كانت جزءاً من العلة التامة .
The Fourth Observatory - The Eighth Topic: Opposing rising and falling motions. The opposition of motions is not due to opposition of what is in it, for rising and falling are undeniably opposites even if what is in them is the same for these two motions, and likewise the motion from black to white is opposite to the motion from white to black even if the path is assumed to be one, i.e., unity of what is in it. (Nor is it due to opposition of the mover) for the opposition of the two natural motions proceeding from a single nature: for air, when it occurs in the region of earth, rises from it naturally, and when it occurs in the region of fire, descends from it likewise, so between these rising and falling there is opposition with unity of the mover. And this example is only valid if extreme difference is not considered in opposition, as appears from the words of the Imam in al-Mulakhkhas and what is mentioned in The Heavens and the World from the book al-Shifa that these two motions are not opposites as some thought, because they end at a single limit. Its explanation according to what is in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya is that opposites must have extreme distance between them, and that is not found in these two motions, because the distance between the motion of fire and the motion of earth is greater than the distance between the rising of air from the center and its descent from the circumference. And how can they be opposites when they aim for a single state, which is to be above water and below fire? And it is objected that it necessarily follows that there would be no opposition in locative motions except the rising that reaches the circumference and the falling that reaches the center, so the motion of a stone would not be [opposed]. It is possible that opposition in some instances is due to opposition of what is in it and what is to it, and in some instances due to opposition of what is in it, or the mover, or the moved. These two objections only apply if the intention were to infer from the absence of opposition due to the mentioned things in some instances to its existence in all instances because of opposition of what is in it and what is to it. Rather, the intention is to explain the reality and ascertain that every instance in which opposition occurs between motions is not without opposition of what is from and what is to it, whether another opposition accompanies it or not. His saying: (And if the path is assumed to be one) meaning that the path from white to black and from increase to decrease is exactly the path from black to white and from decrease to increase; in short, they are the same intermediates, just as the distance in descent is the distance in ascent—thus in al-Shifa. His saying: they end at a single limit, so there is no opposition between them in respect of the endpoint. It is necessary [that opposition of the two motions be from both the starting point and the endpoint]. All opposition of that instance is due to another cause. And by this the defect is shown in explaining the absence of opposition of motions by opposition of the moved, and in explaining the absence of their opposition by opposition of the mover. The answer: It is established from their rules that the verbal noun when added is among the forms of generality, so the meaning is: all opposition of motions is not due to opposition of what is in it. Thus the proof matches the claim. If you say: The absence of this universal affirmative does not entail that the motions are in respect of what is from and what is to, I say: No one claimed this entailment; rather, the matter is in reality as indicated by induction, so ponder. His saying: (from a single nature) for nature is the efficient cause of motion, and the non-appropriate state is not part of the efficient cause, and therefore he did not mention it here, although it is part of the complete cause.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a proof and argumentation. It first states the claim: the opposition of motions is not due to opposition of the substrate (mā fīhi) nor due to opposition of the mover (al-muḥarrik). Evidence: rising and falling are opposites even when the substance (e.g., air) is the same, and the motion from black to white is opposite to that from white to black even if the path is identical. Also, natural motions from a single nature (like air rising from earth's region and falling from fire's region) are opposites despite the same mover. The passage then addresses an objection from a contrary view (al-Rāzī and Ibn Sīnā) that these motions are not truly opposites because they end at one limit (being above water and below fire), so they lack extreme distance. The objection is countered: if that were required, then only motions reaching the circumference and center would be opposites, excluding many like the motion of a stone. The commentary further explains that the real cause of opposition is the opposition of what is from and what is to (mā minhu wa mā ilayhi). A final note clarifies that the nature is the efficient cause, and the non-appropriate state is not part of the efficient cause but of the complete cause.

Key Terms

ما فيه
المحرك
ما منه وما إليه
غاية الخلاف
طبيعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many think that opposition between motions always requires extreme difference in endpoints (like fire and earth).
Correction: The passage shows that opposition can exist without extreme difference, as in rising and falling air which share a common endpoint (above water and below fire). The true cause is the opposition of the from- and to-points.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary cause of opposition between two motions?
A) The difference in the moving substance
B) The difference in the mover
C) The opposition of the from- and to-points (mā minhu wa mā ilayhi)
D) The presence of extreme difference between endpoints

Key Takeaway
The opposition of motions is ultimately due to the opposition of their starting and ending points (mā minhu wa mā ilayhi), not the substrate or the mover.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your daily actions—prayer, work, speech—are motions of the soul. Are they opposites? What are their termini? Do they begin from your ego or from obedience to Allah? And where do they end: in this world or the next? Pause today and trace one action from its start to its end. Is it moving toward Allah or away from Him? Commit to redirect one action whose terminus is worldly toward the Hereafter.
?
The passage shows that even with the same mover (your own will) and the same substrate (your body), actions can be opposed because of their ends. Your love for fame and your love for Allah may both arise from you, but they lead to opposite destinations. Which love moves you more right now? Be honest: what is the true mā ilayhi of your heart's motion? Resolve to examine your intentions before every major action this week.

Causality and Created Things

Opposing Motions from a Single Nature: The Condition for True Opposition
Analyzes the example of air's motions and establishes the condition for opposition in motions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why opposing motions from a single nature require opposition in the source and goal (mā min-hu wa-mā ilay-hi), not merely opposition in the mover.

Core Idea
For motions to be truly opposite, their 'from-which' and 'to-which' must be opposite.

This passage examines a classic problem: can a single nature produce truly opposite motions? Using the example of air, which rises from earth and descends from fire, the author shows that apparent opposition requires deeper analysis. He sets forth the key condition that genuine opposition in motions depends on opposition in their source and destination, not just in the mover.

Guided Path
1
Understand the example
Read the passage describing air's two natural motions. Note that the same nature (air) moves up from earth and down from fire, appearing opposed with one mover.
2
Identify the objection
The objection argues these motions are not truly opposite because they end at the same endpoint (above water, under fire). Find this in the source.
The objection comes from al-Mulakhkhas and al-Shifa.
3
Learn the condition for opposition
The response establishes that true opposition requires opposition in both the starting point and the endpoint. See how the author explains this.
This is the key condition: تضاد ما منه وما إليه.
4
Consider the generalization
The passage then generalizes: all opposition of motions is due to opposition in source and goal, not merely the mover or moved.
Note the precision about the claim being about reality, not logical entailment.
5
Reflect on the efficient cause
The commentary reminds that nature is the efficient cause, and the non-appropriate state is not part of the efficient cause.
This clarifies why only nature (not the environment) is considered the mover.

The Fourth Observatory - The Eighth Intent: The Opposing Motions, the Ascending and Descending. The whiteness to blackness even if the oneness of the path is assumed, meaning the oneness of what is in it, (and not due to opposition of the mover) for the opposition of the two natural motions issuing from a single nature. For air, when it occurs in the space of earth, rises from it by nature, and when it occurs in the space of fire, descends from it likewise. So between these ascending and descending motions there is opposition despite the unity of the mover. This example is only valid if the ultimate difference is not considered in opposition, as appears from the words of the Imam in al-Mulakhkhas and what is mentioned in the Heaven and the World from the book al-Shifa, that these two motions are not opposites as some thought, because they end at one end. Its explanation according to what is in al-Mabahith al-Mashriqiyya is that opposites must have between them ultimate distance, and that is not found in these two motions, because the distance between the motion of fire and the motion of earth is greater than the distance between the air's rising from the center and its descending from the circumference. And how can they be opposites while what is sought by them is a single state, that it be above water and under fire? And it is objected to him that from this it follows that there is no opposition in spatial motions except the ascending reaching the circumference and the descending reaching the center. So the stone's motion between [؟] is not? Then it is possible that opposition in some forms is due to opposition of what is in it and what to it, and in some opposition what is in it or the mover or the moved. These two objections would only arise if the purpose was to infer from the negation of opposition due to the mentioned matters in some forms to its affirmation in all forms, due to opposition of what is in it and what to it. Rather, the purpose is to state the reality and verify it, that every form in which opposition is realized between motions is not without opposition of what from it and what to it, whether there is with it another opposition or not. His statement: (And if the oneness of the path is assumed) that the path from whiteness to blackness and from increase to decrease is the very path from blackness to whiteness and from decrease to increase; in short, they are the same intermediates, just as the distance in descent is the distance in ascent, as in al-Shifa. His statement: they end at one end, so there is no opposition between them in terms of the endpoint, and it is necessary that the opposition of the two motions be in both the beginning and the end. All opposition of that form is by another cause. And by this it becomes clear what defect there is in explaining the negation of opposition of motions by the opposition of the moved, and in explaining the negation of its opposition by the opposition of the mover. The answer is that it has been established from their rules that the masdar mudaf (verbal noun construct) is from the forms of generality, so the meaning is: all opposition of motions is not due to opposition of what is in it. Thus the proof applies to the claim. For if you say: the negation of this universal affirmative does not entail that motions are according to what from them and what to them, I say: no one claimed this entailment; rather, the matter in reality is so, as induction indicates, so let it be pondered. His statement: (from a single nature) for nature is the efficient cause of motion, and the non-appropriate state is not part of the efficient cause, therefore it is not mentioned here, though it is part of the complete cause.
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage begins by presenting an example of natural motions from a single nature: air rising from Earth's region and descending from Fire's region, which appear opposed despite a single mover (nature). It then raises an objection from al-Mulakhkhas and al-Shifa that these motions may not be truly opposed because they aim for the same state (above water, under fire). The response clarifies that true opposition requires opposition in the 'from which' and 'to which' (ما منه وما إليه), not merely in the mover. The author then explains the rule that all opposition of motions is due to opposition in the source and goal, and addresses a potential misunderstanding about the generality of the statement. Finally, a commenter notes that nature is the efficient cause of motion, and the non-appropriate state is not part of the efficient cause. The passage thus establishes the key condition for opposition in motions.

Correction: A single nature (mover) can produce apparently opposite motions; true opposition requires opposition in the starting point and ending point, not just in the mover.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have felt pulled between comfort and growth, or between worldly gain and closeness to Allah. According to this lesson, can those opposing desires be truly opposite if they are both aimed at your own pleasure? What might that reveal about the sincerity of your intentions?
?
When you find yourself doing two different things that appear contradictory (e.g., seeking knowledge but also wasting time), are you truly changed in your starting point and goal, or are you just changing actions while remaining attached to the same worldly goal? Examine one specific conflict in your life.
?
Consider a conflict you have with someone else. Is it rooted in a genuine difference in ultimate objectives (pleasing Allah vs. pleasing self) or merely a difference in means? How can you examine your heart to see if your real goal is the same as theirs—just expressed differently?

The True Cause of Opposition in Motions: Direction
Enumerates incorrect causes and identifies direction as the true cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the true cause of opposition in motions is direction, not the mover, moved object, time, or endpoints.

Core Idea
Direction, not mover or time, determines the opposition of motions.

This passage examines common misconceptions about what makes two motions opposite. It systematically rules out four candidates—the mover, the moved object, time, and the endpoints—and concludes that the opposition stems from the direction in which the motion is oriented. Understanding this refines how we analyze causality in kalam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the repetitive structure: each candidate is introduced with 'nor due to' and then refuted.
The passage uses negation to eliminate false causes.
2
Identify the four rejected causes
List the mover, moved object, time, and endpoints. For each, note the counterexample given (e.g., stone's motions opposite despite same mover/moved).
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage ends with 'بل تضاد الحركات للتوجه'. Understand why direction uniquely satisfies the conditions of difference in type and succession on one subject.
Direction is a property that can truly cause opposition without the problems of the other candidates.

بين الحركات الموجودة تضاد (بل) تضاد الحركات ( للتوجه) قوله : ( فلا تكون حركة الحجر إلخ فيه أن كلتا الحركتين متوجهتان إلى نقطة المركز والمحيط، وإن لم يتحقق الوصول فبينهما غاية الخلاف من حيث التوجه بخلاف صعود الهواء من المركز وهبوطه عن المحيط . قوله : ( بين الحركات الموجودة (تضاد أي حال وجود بل بعده انقطاعها وانعدامها فيه بحث لأن الحركات حال الوصول إلى المنتهى موجودة في أزمنتها متصفة بالتضاد في تلك الحال، نعم إنها غير موصوفة بالتضاد في أثناء المسافة لعدم وجودها بتمامها فالصواب أن يعلل عدم تضاد الحركات بتضاد ما منه وما إليه). قوله : (مع أنهم صرحوا (بخلافه أي صرحوا بالتضاد الحقيقي وليس المراد أنهم صرحوا بالتضاد مطلقا وإلا فيجوز أن يحمل على التضاد المشهور، ولا منافاة وقد يجاب عن الرد بأن تضاد الحركة لتضاد ما منه وما إليه ليس من حيث الحصول فيهما ، إذ لا حركة حينئذ من حيث التوجه، فيعتبر حال الجهة وجهتا العلو والسفل متميزتان بالطبع مختلفتان بالنوع متضادتان بعارض لازم هو غاية القرب من المحيط وغاية البعد عنه بخلاف سائر الجهات، فتأمل . قوله : ( لأن حركة الحجر (إلخ لأن المتحرك جسم ولا تضاد فيه بالذات إذ لا موضوع له . ولو اعتبرنا التضاد بالعرض فقد يكون متضاداً مع تماثل الحركتين كحركة الحار والبارد مثل النار والماء إلى العلو . قوله : ( ولا يمكن توارده لأنه إما على سبيل التعاقب أو على سبيل الاجتماع وكل منهما زمان لا يتصور للزمان : بان .
The Fourth Observatory - The Eighth Intent: The Opposing Motions between the Ascending and Descending by force to above and his motion by nature to below are opposites while they explicitly stated otherwise? (and) due to opposition of the two forced motions like the ascending and descending issuing from one compeller, and not due to opposition of the moved because the stone's motion by force to above and by nature to below are opposites while the moved is one, and not due to opposition of time for there is no opposition in time, i.e., in time (since there is no diversity in it, rather all times are equal in essence) and it cannot be applied (i.e., time's application) to one subject, and for opposites difference in type and succession on one subject are necessary. And because it is an accident of motion, and opposition of accidents is not opposition of substances. So if opposition in time were assumed, it would not necessitate opposition of motions. And not due to obtaining in the endpoints, which are the beginnings and ends of motions, because obtaining in the endpoints is non-existent during the existence of motion. For obtaining at the beginning occurs before it and ceases at its time, and obtaining at the end occurs after it. So if opposition were due to obtaining in the endpoints, there would be no opposition between existing motions. Rather, opposition of motions is due to direction. His statement: (so the stone's motion, etc.) in it that both motions are directed to the point of the center and the circumference, even if arrival is not realized, so between them is ultimate difference in terms of direction, unlike the air's rising from the center and its descending from the circumference. His statement: (between the existing motions opposition, i.e., in the state of existence, but after their cessation and non-existence) in it there is a discussion because motions at the time of arrival at the endpoint exist in their times described with opposition in that state, yes they are not described with opposition during the distance due to their not existing in their entirety, so the correct thing is to explain the absence of opposition of motions by opposition of what from them and what to them). His statement: (while they explicitly stated otherwise) i.e., they explicitly stated real opposition, and it is not meant that they stated opposition absolutely, otherwise it is permissible to interpret it as the well-known opposition, and there is no contradiction. And it may be answered against the objection that opposition of motion due to opposition of what from it and what to it is not in terms of obtaining in them, for there is no motion then in terms of direction, so the state of direction is considered, and the two directions of height and depth are naturally distinct, different in type, opposed by a necessary accident which is the utmost nearness to the circumference and the utmost distance from it, unlike other directions, so ponder. His statement: (because the stone's motion, etc.) because the moved is a body and there is no opposition in it in essence since it has no subject. And if we consider opposition accidentally, it may be opposite while the two motions are similar, like the motion of the hot and cold such as fire and water upward. His statement: (and it cannot be applied) because it is either successively or simultaneously, and both are time but cannot be conceived for time: it became clear.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a classification and refutation of incorrect causes for opposition in motions. It first lists the factors that are mistakenly thought to cause opposition: the mover, the moved object, time, and the endpoints. For each, it provides a counterexample: forced motions from a single compeller can be opposite; the stone's forced upward and natural downward motions are opposite despite a single moved body; time has no diversity to cause opposition; and endpoints are absent during motion. The passage then concludes that the true cause is direction (التوجه). The commentary that follows elaborates on these points, clarifying that the real opposition is due to the direction of motion toward opposite ends (e.g., center vs. circumference), and that the from/to (ما منه وما إليه) is ultimately linked to direction. It also addresses an objection about explicit statements of opposition, and notes that the moved body itself has no inherent opposition.

توجه
تضاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Opposition of motions requires the mover or the moved object to be opposite.
Correction: The same mover and same moved object can produce opposite motions, so opposition is not due to them but to direction.

Checkpoint

A) The mover
B) The moved object
C) Time
D) Direction (التوجه)

Key Takeaway
Opposition in motions is ultimately caused by direction, not by the mover, moved object, time, or endpoints.

Actual vs. Assumed Beginning and End in Motion
Explains distinction between actual and assumed beginning/end in straight vs circular motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between actual and assumed beginnings and ends in rectilinear and circular motion, and the conditions under which each applies.

Core Idea
In motion, beginnings and ends can be actual or merely assumed; rectilinear motion has actual ones, circular motion often only assumed.

This passage from a classical kalam text explores a key distinction: whether the start and end points of motion are real or just conceptual. The author contrasts rectilinear motion, which always has actual endpoints, with circular motion, where endpoints are usually assumed unless the motion is finite. Understanding this helps clarify foundational concepts in physics and metaphysics.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then the English translation. Notice the author's precise distinctions.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the two motion types
Find where the author discusses rectilinear motion (actual beginning/end) and circular motion (assumed beginning/end). Note the reasoning.
3
Examine special cases
Look for the discussion on positional motion and eternal motion. How do these affect the actuality of beginning and end?
This step clarifies apparent contradictions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المحيط، فإنهما متقدمان على وجود الحركة ومقتضيان لكون الحركتين متضادتين كما عرفت ( وذلك ) أي اتصاف أحدهما بكونه مبدأ والآخر بكونه منتهى (قد يكون بالفعل كما في الحركة المستقيمة ) فإن لها مبدأ متصفاً بالمبدائية بالفعل ولها كذلك (و) قد يكون ذلك الاتصاف ) بمجرد الفرض كما في الحركة المستديرة فإن أي جزء فرضت على الجسم المتحرك بالاستدارة كالفلك ( مبدأ للدور ومنتهى له باعتبارين) إذ الحركة عن كل جزء هي بعينها الحركة إلى ذلك الجزء فلا مبدأ ولا منتهى للمستديرة إلا بمجرد الفرض ( ولا تمايز فيه ) أي في الدائر حتى يثبت للدور ابتداء وانتهاء بالفعل (إلا) بما يعرض من موازاة أو فرض أو غير ذلك) من الشروق والغروب، وليس شيء منها موجبا للتمايز الخارجي، وليس من شرط وجود الحركة المستديرة أن يوجد هناك نقطة بالفعل لتكون مبدأ من وجه ومنتهى من وجه وإلا امتنع حركة الفلك بالاستدارة إذ لا وجود للنقطة بالفعل إلا بسبب القطع وهو عليه محال عندهم، بل يكفي لتحقق المستديرة كون النقطة بالقوة القريبة وهاهنا بحث وهو أن الحركة المستديرة حركة وضعية فيكون مبدؤها وكذا منتهاها وضعاً مخصوصاً، كما أن مبدأ الحركة الكيفية ومنتهاها كيف مخصوص فإذا فرض أن جسماً كان ساكناً ثم تحرك على نفسه، فالوضع الذي ابتدأت الحركة منه كان مبدأ لها، وإذا فرض سكونها ثانياً كان الوضع الذي انقطعت الحركة عنده منتهي لها سواء كان مماثلا للوضع الأول أو مخالفا له فقد ثبت للمستديرة مبدأ ومنتهى بالفعل كالمستقيمة نعم إذا فرض أن المستديرة أزلية أبدية كما هو مذهبهم في الحركات الفلكية لم يكن هناك مبدأ ولا منتهى بالفعل كما نبهناك عليه فيما سلف ولا يمكن مثل هذا الفرض في المستقيمة لتناهي الأبعاد وانقطاع الحركة بالرجوع والانعطاف فلا بد لها دائماً من مبدأ ومنتهى بالفعل، نعم إذا فرض أن جسماً تحرك على محيط دائرة حتى تمم دورة كان مبدؤها ومنتهاها واحداً بالذات مختلفاً بالاعتبار، إلا أن هذه حركة أينية في الاصطلاح مستديرة بحسب اللغة
The surrounding [circle], for they are prior to the existence of motion and necessitate that the two motions are opposite as you know. (That is) the qualification of one of them as a beginning and the other as an end (may be actual as in rectilinear motion) for it has a beginning actually qualified as beginning, and likewise (it may be that qualification) by mere assumption as in circular motion, for any part you assume on the body moving circularly like the sphere (is a beginning of the rotation and an end of it under two aspects) because the motion from each part is identical to the motion to that part, so there is no beginning nor end for circular motion except by mere assumption. (And there is no distinction in it) i.e. in the circle such that the rotation would have an actual beginning and end (except) by what occurs of alignment or assumption or other things) like sunrise and sunset, and none of these necessitate external distinction, and it is not a condition for the existence of circular motion that there be an actual point to be a beginning in one respect and an end in another, otherwise the circular motion of the sphere would be impossible, because there is no existence of a point actually except by cutting, and that is impossible according to them. Rather, for the realization of circular motion, it suffices that the point be in proximate potentiality. And here there is a discussion: namely that circular motion is a positional motion, so its beginning and likewise its end are a specific position, just as the beginning of qualitative motion and its end are a specific quality. So if it is assumed that a body was at rest then moved upon itself, then the position from which the motion began is its beginning, and if its rest is assumed secondly, then the position at which the motion ceased is its end, whether it is similar to the first position or different from it. So circular motion has been proven to have an actual beginning and end like rectilinear motion. Yes, if it is assumed that the circular motion is eternal perpetual as is their doctrine regarding celestial motions, then there is no actual beginning nor end as we alerted you to previously, and such an assumption is not possible in rectilinear motion because of the finitude of dimensions and the cessation of motion by regression and curvature, so it necessarily always has an actual beginning and end. Yes, if it is assumed that a body moves on the circumference of a circle until it completes a revolution, then its beginning and its end are one in essence, different in consideration, except that this is local motion (haraka ayniyya) in terminology, circular in language.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage discusses whether the beginning (mabda') and end (muntaha) of motion are actual or merely assumed. It begins by stating that the qualification of one thing as a beginning and another as an end can be actual, as in rectilinear motion, where the start point and end point are actual. In circular motion, however, any point on the circle can be taken as both beginning and end depending on consideration, so the qualification is only by assumption. The author then notes that for circular motion to exist, it is not necessary to have an actual point; potential proximity suffices. A discussion follows: circular motion is positional (haraka wad'iyya), so its beginning and end are specific positions. If a body moves from a rest position, that position is the actual beginning, and if it returns to rest, that position is the actual end, making the beginning and end actual like rectilinear motion. However, if the circular motion is eternal (as in celestial spheres), there is no actual beginning or end. Rectilinear motion, due to finite dimensions, always has an actual beginning and end. Finally, if a body completes a full circle, the beginning and end are one in essence but different in consideration, but this is local motion (haraka ayniyya) in terminology, circular in language.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Circular motion never has actual beginning or end.
Correction: The passage explains that circular motion can have actual beginning and end when it is finite and positional (e.g., starting from rest). Only eternal circular motion lacks actual beginning/end.

Checkpoint

A) Always, because every motion has actual endpoints.
B) Only when it is assumed to be eternal.
C) When it is finite and positional, e.g., starting from rest.
D) Never, because circular motion is continuous.

Key Takeaway
Rectilinear motion necessarily has actual beginning and end, while circular motion's beginning and end are usually by assumption, except when the motion is finite and positional.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the assumption that your life's motion is like a straight line—with a clear beginning and end. But have you been living as though your days are a continuous circle, with no real start or finish to your responsibilities? Where in your daily routine have you lost sight of actual beginnings and ends, causing you to delay repentance or good deeds as if you have endless time? What would it take for you to treat each action as having a real beginning and an actual end—like the rectilinear motion the author describes—and to act with urgency?
?
The author states that only eternal celestial motions lack actual beginning and end. Your life is not eternal—it has a definite start (birth) and will have an end (death). Are you living as if your life's motion is assumed and endless, delaying repentance and good deeds? How does recognizing that your existence has an actual beginning and an end change what you will do today?
?

What is the 'rest' you need to break from to make that sin's motion finite? What beginning will you set today to end that cycle, and how will you mark that moment as an actual end to that pattern?

Basis of Opposition of Ascending and Descending Motions
Clarifies that opposition of motions is due to beginning/end concepts, not spatial nearness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the opposition of ascending and descending motions is based on the directionality of beginning and end, not on spatial proximity.

Core Idea
Opposition of motions arises from opposite 'from' and 'to', not nearness.

This brief note from a classical kalam text clarifies a subtle point about motion: two motions can be opposite even if they occur close together. The key is not their spatial positions but their inherent directionality—what they start from and what they aim toward. Let's read the original text and unpack its meaning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic note
Start by reading the Arabic passage aloud or silently. Notice its concise style and key terms like 'مبدأ' (beginning) and 'منتهى' (end).
The passage is a 'tanbih' (note) so it's highlighting an important nuance.
2
Identify the core argument
The author states that opposition comes from 'ما منه' and 'ما إليه' (from which and to which) being opposite in 'مبدئية' and 'منتهية' (beginningness and endness). Contrast this with the alternative view that it is due to extreme proximity or distance.
The text explicitly rejects spatial considerations as irrelevant.
3
Connect to the common misunderstanding
Reflect on why someone might think distance matters. The note helps us see that motions are defined by their direction, not by how near or far they are spatially.
This reinforces a key principle in kalam: causality is tied to intrinsic qualities, not accidental relations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه . المبدأ مبدأ الحركة الواحدة والآخر عرض له منتهى فإنه صريح في أن تضاد الصاعدة والهابطة باعتبار كون ما منه وما إليه فيهما مضاداً ومخالفاً للآخر في المبدئية والمنتهية لا باعتبار أنه في غاية القرب أو في غاية البعد فإنه لا تعلق لهذين الاعتبارين بالحركة فضلاً عن أن يكون موجباً للتضاد . قوله : ( وهاهنا بحث إلخ ) مقصوداً لقائل إذا فرض ابتداء المستدبرة من نقطة كما يفرضون الدور بعينه كان المبدأ والمنتهى بمجرد الفرض لا أن الحركة الوضعية مبدؤها ومنتهاها النقطة حتى يرد ما ذكره الشارح
A note. The beginning is the beginning of a single motion and the other [motion] has an end. It is explicit that the opposition of ascending and descending [motions] is in virtue of the fact that their 'from which' and 'to which' are opposite and contrary to the other in beginningness and endness, not in virtue of it being at extreme proximity or extreme distance, for these two considerations have no connection to motion, let alone causing opposition. His statement: (and here there is a discussion etc.) is intended for one who says: if the beginning of the [motion] starting from a point is assumed, just as they assume the rotation itself, then the beginning and end are by mere assumption, not that the positional motion has its beginning and end as the point, such that what the commentator mentioned would be rebutted.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This is a note (tanbih) clarifying the basis of opposition between ascending and descending motions. It states that the beginning (mabda') of one motion and the end (muntaha) of the other are what make them opposite. It emphasizes that the opposition is due to the concepts of 'from which' and 'to which' being opposite in terms of being a beginning versus an end, not because one is extremely near and the other extremely far. Such spatial considerations are irrelevant to motion and cannot cause opposition. The note then references a previous discussion: if one assumes a starting point for a rotation, then the beginning and end are only by assumption, and the positional motion's beginning and end are not the point itself, contrary to what some might claim.

ما إليه

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that opposition of ascending and descending motions is due to the spatial distance between them (extreme nearness or farness).
Correction: The note clarifies that opposition is due to the 'from which' and 'to which' being opposite in beginningness and endness, not due to spatial considerations.

Checkpoint

A) Extreme nearness or distance.
B) The concepts of 'from which' and 'to which' being opposite in beginningness and endness.
C) The speed of the motions.
D) The weight of the moving bodies.

Key Takeaway
The opposition of ascending and descending motions is rooted in the opposite directionality of their beginnings and ends, not their spatial proximity.

Why Circular Motion Is Not Opposite to Straight Motion
Denies abstract circularity and proves circular movement is not opposite to straight movement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why abstract circularity does not exist and why circular motion cannot be opposite to straight motion.

Core Idea
Circular motion and straight motion are not opposites because abstract circularity is impossible.

In this lesson, we examine a key argument from Ilm al-Kalam about the nature of motion. The author denies the existence of abstract circularity and demonstrates that circular movement is not the opposite of straight movement. This clarifies an important aspect of the physics underlying theological arguments.

Guided Path
1
Understand the denial of abstract circularity
Read the first part of the passage where the author states that only specific circular things exist, not an abstract circularity.
Abstract circularity would be 'circularity as such' independent of any particular circular object.
2
Grasp why no specific circular thing is opposite
Notice the reasoning: all circular motions share the same beginning and end, so none is more deserving to be opposite of straight motion.
Straight motion has a different beginning and end, so no circular motion can be singled out as opposite.
3
Learn the requirement of succession
The author argues that opposites must alternate on the same subject. Circular motion cannot succeed straight motion on the subject, so it cannot be an opposite.
This is a logical requirement for any two things to be considered opposites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المرصد الرابع - المقصد الثامن : الحركات المتضادة بين الصاعدة والهابطة نقول : لا وجود للاستدارة المجردة، إنما الموجود في الخارج ما هو مستدير معين ولا شيء من المستديرات المعينة أولى بالمضادة لما عرفت ولما امتنع حصول الاستدارة المجردة في الخارج امتنع معاقبتها للمستقيم في الموضوع، فلا يكون ضداً له قوله : ( للاستدارة المجردة أي المستديرة من حيث هو لما عرفت من تشارك الكل في المبدأ والمنتهى المخالفين لمبدأ المستقيمة ومنتهاها، وكل ما هو يفرض ضداً كان ما هو أكثر تحدبا أولى به فلا يكون شيء منها أولى قوله: (ولما امتنع إلخ) وجه آخر لعدم كون المستديرة من حيث طبيعتها ضداً للمستقيمة إذ لا بد في الضدين من تعاقبهما على موضوع واحد وإذا لم يقع المستديرة موجوداً على موضوع المستقيمة.
The Fourth Observation - The Eighth Topic: The Contradictory Movements between the Ascending and Descending. We say: There is no existence for abstract circularity. Rather, what exists in the external is a specific circular thing, and no specific circular thing is more deserving of being opposite, as you have known. And since the attainment of abstract circularity in the external is impossible, its succeeding the straight in the subject is impossible, so it is not an opposite to it. His saying: (For abstract circularity i.e. the circular insofar as it is circular, because you have known that all share in the beginning and the end which are different from the beginning of the straight and its end, and everything that is assumed to be opposite, what is more curved is more deserving of it, so nothing of them is more deserving. His saying: (And since it is impossible etc.) Another aspect for the non-opposition of the circular by its nature to the straight, because for two opposites there must be their succession upon one subject, and since the circular does not occur as existing upon the subject of the straight.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage presents two arguments against the claim that circular movement is the opposite of straight movement. First, it denies the existence of abstract circularity (al-istidārah al-mujarradah) in the external world; only specific circular things exist, and no specific circular thing has priority in being opposite, because all circular motions share the same beginning and end, which are different from those of straight motion. Therefore, none is more deserving to be opposite. Second, even if abstract circularity existed, it could not succeed straight motion in the same subject, which is a requirement for two opposites. The commentary clarifies that the first point relies on the shared beginning and end, and the second point emphasizes that opposites must alternate on the same subject, which circular motion cannot do.

Key Terms
استدارة مجردة
مضادة
مستقيمة
مستديرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that abstract circularity exists in the external world and that any circular motion can be opposite to straight motion.
Correction: The passage argues that abstract circularity does not exist; only specific circular things exist. Moreover, for two things to be opposite, they must alternate on the same subject, which circular motion cannot do.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is no specific circular thing more deserving of being the opposite of straight motion?
A) Because all circular motions have the same beginning and end.
B) Because circular motions are more curved.
C) Because circular motions cannot succeed straight motion.
D) Because abstract circularity does not exist.

Key Takeaway
Abstract circularity does not exist, and circular motion cannot succeed straight motion in the same subject, so it is not an opposite.

Circular Movements Cannot Be Contradictory
Proves circular movements are not contradictory via infinite regress of opposites.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why circular movements cannot be mutually contradictory according to kalam reasoning, specifically that it would entail an infinite number of opposites for a single movement.

Core Idea
Circular movements oppose each other only if their endpoints conflict, but shared endpoints avoid contradiction.

This passage extends the previous discussion from straight and circular movements to circular movements among themselves. The author argues that if circular movements were contradictory, then a single circular movement would require infinitely many opposites—an absurd outcome. The commentary adds a nuance about the scope of the proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once to get the flow, then read the literal translation. Notice the logical structure: a conditional argument leading to an absurdity.
The passage is dense; take your time.
2
Identify the key premise and conclusion
The author states that contradiction between movements arises from contradiction of their beginnings and ends. Then he assumes contradiction among circular movements and deduces an infinite chain of opposites, which he rejects.
This is a reductio ad absurdum argument.
3
Understand the infinite regress
Because two endpoints of an arc can be shared by infinitely many arcs, if each such arc represented a distinct opposite movement, a single circular movement would have infinitely many opposites—impossible.
4
Consider the commentator's qualification
The commentator notes that the proof does not apply to a movement on a specific arc with fixed endpoints, where reversal does not produce contradiction. Reflect on why this nuance matters.
This shows the proof's limits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ولا) تضاد المستديرة المستديرة لنحو ذلك الذي ذكر لنفي التضاد بين المستقيمة والمستديرة فإن التضاد بين الحركات لتضاد مباديها وغاياتها، فلو كان بين المستديرات تضاد لكان لمستديرة واحدة أضداد غير متناهية متخالفة بالنوع، وذلك لأن طرفي مستديرة واحدة قد يكونان طرفين لدوائر أي لقسي غير متناهية فإنه يجوز اشتراك قسي غير متناهية في طرفين فلو كانت المستديرة ضداً للمستديرة لكان لمستديرة واحدة أضداد بلا نهاية هي المستديرات الموجهة من منتهى تلك المستديرة إلى مبدئها وهو باطل قوله : ( لأن طرفي مستديرة إلخ) هذا الدليل أخص من المدعى لأنه لا يجري في المستديرة الواقعة على قوس معين من مبدأ ومنتهى معين، والحركة الواقعة عليها بالعكس مع أنه لا تضاد بينهما كما عرفت منقولاً من الشفاء. تحققه بينهم بين الأنواع الأخيرة المندرجة تحيت جنس قريب، إلا أن يحمل كلامهم على تحققه فيما بين أفراد الأنواع الأخيرة .
(And not) the contradiction of the circular to the circular is like that which was mentioned to negate the contradiction between the straight and the circular, for contradiction between movements is due to the contradiction of their beginnings and ends. So if there were contradiction among circular movements, then for a single circular movement there would be infinitely many opposites different in species. That is because the two endpoints of a single circular movement may be endpoints for infinitely many circles, i.e., arcs, for it is permissible that infinitely many arcs share two endpoints. So if a circular movement were opposite to a circular movement, then for one circular movement there would be infinite opposites, which are the circular movements directed from the end of that circular movement to its beginning, and this is false. His saying: (Because the two endpoints of a circular movement etc.) This proof is more specific than the claim, because it does not apply to the circular movement occurring on a specific arc with a specific beginning and end, and the movement occurring on it in reverse, while there is no contradiction between them, as you have known, transmitted from al-Shifā. Its realization among them among the last species included under a proximate genus, unless their speech is interpreted as its realization among individuals of the last species.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage provides a proof that circular movements are not contradictory to each other. The reason is that contradiction between movements arises from contradiction of their beginnings and ends. If there were contradiction among circular movements, then a single circular movement would have infinitely many opposites of different species, because the same two endpoints can be shared by infinitely many arcs (any arc with the same start and end points). This would lead to an absurd infinite regress. The commentator notes that this proof is more specific than the general claim, as it does not apply to a circular movement on a specific arc with specific endpoints, which when reversed does not exhibit contradiction, as cited from al-Shifā. The final sentence discusses the realization of this among species under a common genus.

Correction: The passage shows that direction alone does not make circular movements contradictory; contradiction requires opposition of beginnings and ends, and circular movements share endpoints, leading to infinite regress if they were contradictory.

Movements to Succession and Its Opposite Are Not Contradictory
Shows that clockwise and counterclockwise movements are not opposites due to equal halves and endpoints.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why clockwise and counterclockwise movements in a celestial sphere are not truly contradictory, because they perform the same function in alternating halves due to the sphere's homogeneity.

Core Idea
Opposite directions do not imply contradiction in a homogeneous sphere.

At first glance, clockwise and counterclockwise motions seem opposite and contradictory. However, this passage argues that careful analysis shows they are not. Using the celestial sphere as an example, it demonstrates that both motions achieve the same endpoint (e.g., descending from Cancer to Capricorn) but traverse different halves. Since the sphere is simple and its parts identical, the halves are equivalent, so no contradiction arises.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the example with zodiac signs.
Pay attention to the terms 'حركة إلى التوالي' and 'حركة إلى خلافه'.
2
Identify the two movements
The passage discusses movement 'to succession' (clockwise) and 'to its opposite' (counterclockwise). Find where they are contrasted.
3
Understand the argument of alternating halves
The author shows that each movement does the same action (e.g., descending from Cancer to Capricorn) but in alternating halves of the sphere. This is key to showing they are not contradictory.
The example uses different zodiac signs for each path.
4
Note the reason from the sphere's simplicity
The passage concludes that because the sphere is simple and its parts similar, the halves and endpoints are equal, so no contradiction exists.
This refutes the apparent contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الحركة إلى التوالي والحركة إلى خلافه فكل من هاتين الحركتين تفعل مثل فعل الأخرى ولكن في النصفين على التبادل فإن المنحدر من السرطان إلى الجدي على التوالي يكون مسافته الأسد والسنبلة والميزان والعقرب والقوس والمنحدر من السرطان إلى الجدي لا على التوالي مسافته الجوزاء والثور والحمل والحوت والدلو فقد فعل كل منهما في الانحدار مثل فعل الآخر، أعني الحركة المبعدة عن السرطان الموصلة إلى الجدي، لكن في النصف الآخر، وقس على ذلك حال الصعود من الجدي إلى السرطان، فإنه على عكس الانحدار المذكور، ولما كان الفلك جسماً بسيطاً متشابه الأجزاء كان النصفان متساويين في الماهية وكذلك الأطراف والنهايات متساوية فيها، فلا يكون شيء منها سبباً لتضاد الحركات المستديرة، فلا تكون متضادة قوله : ( وأما الحركة إلى التوالي إلخ) دفع لما يتراءى من كون هاتين الحركتين متضادتين.
As for the movement to the succession and the movement to its opposite, each of these two movements does the like of the action of the other, but in the two halves alternately. For the descender from Cancer to Capricorn in succession has its distance passing through Leo, Virgo, Libra, Scorpio, and Sagittarius; and the descender from Cancer to Capricorn not in succession has its distance passing through Gemini, Taurus, Aries, Pisces, and Aquarius. So each of them in descending does the like of the action of the other, namely the movement moving away from Cancer and reaching Capricorn, but in the other half. And analogize to that the case of the ascent from Capricorn to Cancer, for it is the reverse of the mentioned descent. And since the celestial sphere is a simple body with similar parts, the two halves are equal in essence, and likewise the extremities and ends are equal in it. So nothing of them is a cause for contradiction of circular movements, so they are not contradictory. His saying: (As for the movement to the succession etc.) is a refutation of what appears to be that these two movements are contradictory.

Commentary
This passage addresses the apparent contradiction between a movement 'to the succession' (e.g., clockwise) and 'to its opposite' (counterclockwise). It argues that these two movements are not truly contradictory. Each movement performs the same action (e.g., descending from Cancer to Capricorn) but in alternating halves of the celestial sphere. The example illustrates that the two descents pass through different zodiac signs, yet both achieve the same result: moving away from Cancer and reaching Capricorn. Since the celestial sphere is a simple, homogeneous body, the two halves are essentially identical, and the endpoints (the beginning and end points) are also equal. Therefore, there is no basis for contradiction. The commentary notes that this is a refutation of the apparent contradiction between these movements.

Author's Objection and the Verbal Nature of the Dispute
Author's objection and claim that the dispute is verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's objection that the difference between opposing movements is notional rather than real, and why some scholars consider the dispute merely verbal.

Core Idea
Disputes about movement opposites may be merely verbal if 'opposite' is defined differently.

The author raises an objection to the previous claim that movement to succession and its opposite are not contradictory. He insists that the movements in two halves are genuinely different because their beginnings and ends are opposite. The commentator then explains that this difference is notional, not real, and cites al-Mulakhkhas to suggest the entire discussion may be verbal. In this lesson, we will examine the author's objection and the subsequent analysis of whether the opposition is real or verbal.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the layered structure: objection, commentator's explanation, and citation from al-Mulakhkhas.
2
Identify the author's objection
The author objects by saying that movement in two halves, despite unified distance, is different. Find this statement and understand why he says it.
He is arguing against the previous view that the two movements are not ultimately different.
3
Understand notional vs. real opposition
The commentator clarifies that the difference is only by assumption (notional variation) and does not necessitate real contradiction. Recognize the distinction.
Real contradiction requires opposition in essence or by a necessary attribute, like ascending vs. descending.
4
Analyze the two definitions from al-Mulakhkhas
The passage from al-Mulakhkhas offers two definitions of 'opposites.' If opposites are just existential meanings that cannot coexist, then straight and circular movements are opposites. If further conditions are added, they may not be.
This shows the dispute may be merely verbal, depending on definition.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider how the commentator's final remarks on equality of extremities and contradiction between beginnings/ends reinforce the notional nature of the difference.
The contradiction is by virtue of being beginning and end, not by essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال المصنف : ( ولا يخفى ما فيه من أن الحركة في النصفين مع اتحاد المسافة مختلفة ) قوله : ( ولا يخفى إلخ) مقصود ذلك القائل أن الحركتين المذكورتين ليس بينهما غاية الخلاف، إذ يفعل كل منهما بفعل الآخر وتحد غايتها، وإنما عرض الخلاف باعتبار فرض مبدأ كلتيهما ومنتهاه مخالفاً للأخرى وذلك مغايرة اعتبارية لا يوجب تضاد الحركتين كما مر منقولاً من الشفاء. قوله : ( وإن كانا مفروضين قد عرفت أن تغاير المبدأ والمنتهى بالفرض لا التضاد يصحح بينهما ولا بد في تضاد الحركات من تضادهما بالذات أو باعتبار عارض لازم كما في الصاعدة والهابطة. وذكر في الملخص أن أمثال هذه المباحث لفظية لأنه إن أريد بالضدين كل معنيين وجوديين يمتنع اجتماعهما دفعة واحدة في محل واحد كانت الحركة المستقيمة مضادة للمستديرة وكانت المستديرات أيضاً متضادة لامتناع الاجتماع، وإن أريد مع ذلك أن يكون ما منه وما إليه أموراً موجودة قوله : ( وكذلك الأطراف والنهايات متساوية (فيها فإن قلت الأطراف متحدة في المثال المذكور لا متساوية قلت : الحكم بالتساوي مبني على المغايرة الاعتبارية . قوله : ( للتضاد بين المبدأين (والمنتهيين أي باعتبار المبدئية والمنتهية وإن كان ذاتاهما متحدين بالماهية.
The author said: (What is in it is not hidden: that the movement in the two halves with unified distance is different.) His saying: (What is not hidden etc.) The intention of that speaker is that the two mentioned movements do not have the ultimate difference, for each of them does the action of the other and achieves its goal, and the difference only arises by assuming that the beginning of each of them and its end are opposite to the other, and that is a notional variation that does not necessitate contradiction of the two movements, as has been transmitted from al-Shifā. His saying: (And if they are assumed, you have known that the variation of beginning and end by assumption does not establish contradiction between them, and for contradiction of movements it is necessary that they be contradictory in essence or by a necessary attribute, as in the ascending and descending.) And it was mentioned in al-Mulakhkhas that such investigations are verbal, because if by 'two opposites' is meant two existential meanings whose simultaneous occurrence in one subject is impossible, then straight movement is opposite to circular movement, and circular movements are also opposite due to impossibility of coexistence; and if it is also meant that the 'from' and 'to' are existent matters... His saying: (And likewise the extremities and ends are equal in it; for if you say the extremities are identical in the mentioned example, not equal, I say: the judgment of equality is based on notional variation.) His saying: (For contradiction between the two beginnings and the two ends, i.e., by virtue of being beginning and end, even if their essences are identical in essence.)
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage contains the author's objection to the previous argument that movement to succession and its opposite are not contradictory. The author points out that the movement in the two halves, despite having a unified distance, is actually different. The commentator explains that the objection is that the two movements do have real difference, because when considering each half together, the beginnings and ends are opposite. The commentator then cites al-Mulakhkhas, which suggests the discussion is merely verbal: if 'opposites' are defined simply as existent things that cannot coexist, then straight and circular movements are opposites, as are circular movements among themselves; but if we additionally require that the 'from' and 'to' are actual existent matters, then the conclusion may differ. The passage concludes with notes on the equality of extremities, stating that equality is based on notional variation, and that contradiction between beginnings and ends is by virtue of their being beginnings and ends, even if their essences are identical.

Correction: The passage clarifies that notional variation (مغايرة اعتبارية) does not necessitate real contradiction; real contradiction requires opposition in essence or by a necessary attribute.

Key Takeaway
